#### # Instructions  
####   
#### A circular buffer, cyclic buffer or ring buffer is a data structure that uses a single, fixed-size buffer as if it were connected end-to-end.  
####   
#### A circular buffer first starts empty and of some predefined length.  
#### For example, this is a 7-element buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Assume that a 1 is written into the middle of the buffer (exact starting location does not matter in a circular buffer):  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Then assume that two more elements are added — 2 & 3 — which get appended after the 1:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][2][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If two elements are then removed from the buffer, the oldest values inside the buffer are removed.  
#### The two elements removed, in this case, are 1 & 2, leaving the buffer with just a 3:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If the buffer has 7 elements then it is completely full:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][3][4]  
#### ```  
####   
#### When the buffer is full an error will be raised, alerting the client that further writes are blocked until a slot becomes free.  
####   
#### When the buffer is full, the client can opt to overwrite the oldest data with a forced write.  
#### In this case, two more elements — A & B — are added and they overwrite the 3 & 4:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### 3 & 4 have been replaced by A & B making 5 now the oldest data in the buffer.  
#### Finally, if two elements are removed then what would be returned is 5 & 6 yielding the buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Because there is space available, if the client again uses overwrite to store C & D then the space where 5 & 6 were stored previously will be used not the location of 7 & 8.  
#### 7 is still the oldest element and the buffer is once again full.  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [C][D][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: circular_buffer.cpp circular_buffer.h  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.  

I understand. We need to implement a circular buffer with specific functionality. Let's break this down:

1. The buffer needs to be fixed-size
2. We need to support reading and writing elements
3. When the buffer is full, normal writes should raise an error
4. We need to support overwriting the oldest elements when forced
5. We need to keep track of the oldest and newest elements

Since this is C++, we'll implement it as a class. Let's add the necessary declarations to the header file and implementations to the source file.

First, let's update the header file to include the class definition:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t head;
    size_t tail;
    size_t count;
    size_t capacity;
    bool full;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t size);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool is_full() const;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

```

Now, let's implement the methods in the source file:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    full = false;
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    count++;
    full = (tail == head);
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        // If the buffer is full, the head needs to be advanced
        read();
    }
    write(data);
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = tail;
    count = 0;
    full = false;
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::empty() const {
    return (!full && (head == tail));
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::is_full() const {
    return full;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for common types
// This ensures the implementation is available at link time
template class circular_buffer<int>;
// Add other types as needed

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    full = false;
    count--;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    count++;
    full = (tail == head);
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        // If the buffer is full, the head needs to be advanced
        read();
    }
    write(data);
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = tail;
    count = 0;
    full = false;
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::empty() const {
    return (!full && (head == tail));
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::is_full() const {
    return full;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for common types
// This ensures the implementation is available at link time
template class circular_buffer<int>;
// Add other types as needed

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), count(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    full = false;
    count--;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (full) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    count++;
    full = (tail == head);
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // If the buffer is full, the head needs to be advanced
        read();
    }
    write(data);
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    count = 0;
    full = false;
}

bool circular_buffer::empty() const {
    return count == 0;
}

bool circular_buffer::is_full() const {
    return count == capacity;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
```

However, there's an issue with the `overwrite` implementation. Let's fix it to properly handle the case where the buffer is full by overwriting the oldest element and advancing the head:

Wait, according to the instructions, when doing a forced write (overwrite), the oldest data should be overwritten, making the next element the oldest.
So when the buffer is full, we write to the current tail position, which will overwrite the oldest element if we also advance the head
But this needs to be done carefully

Here's a better implementation for `overwrite`:

```cpp
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element at head and advance head
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        head = tail; // This makes head and tail equal, which with full=true means buffer is full
        // But according to the example, after overwriting, the buffer remains full
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
```

But this doesn't seem right. Let's think differently. When the buffer is full, writing at tail will overwrite the next element which is also the head
So we need to advance both head and tail
Wait, the tail should always point to the next write position
So when full, write to tail, then advance both head and tail
But head needs to be advanced to point to the new oldest element

Wait, here's a correct implementation:
```cpp
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Write data to current tail, which will overwrite the oldest? No.
        // When buffer is full, head and tail are equal, and head points to the oldest
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        head = tail; // This maintains full=true
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
```

But this doesn't match the example where after overwriting, the oldest element changes
Actually, when overwriting, we should advance head to make space
So:
```cpp
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Read the oldest element to advance head, then write
        // But we can't call read() as it returns a value we don't need
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    }
    // Write the data which will handle updating tail and full flag
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    full = (tail == head);
}
```

This seems better. Let's use this implementation:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {

        // But this needs to be done carefully
        // Let's read and then write, which matches the example
        // But read() will throw if empty, which it's not since full is true
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;

        write(data);
    }

=======
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Make space by moving head forward
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    }
    // Write the data
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    // Update full flag
    full = (tail == head);
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should now correctly handle overwriting by always making space when the buffer is full, and then writing the new data. The head is advanced, which effectively removes the oldest element, making room for the new data.

I see the issue. The implementation of `overwrite` is not correct. When the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element, which is at the head, and then advance both head and tail. But in the current implementation, we're always writing to the tail, which is not correct when the buffer is full.

Let's fix the `overwrite` implementation:

1. When the buffer is full, we write to the current head position and advance both head and tail
2. But this may not be exactly right
3. According to the instructions, when doing a forced write, the oldest data is overwritten, which is at head
4. So we should write to head and advance head, and also advance tail to maintain consistency

Wait, but this seems tricky. Let's think through an example:
Buffer is full: head and tail are at the same position (since it's full)
Overwrite with new data: write to head, advance head, and advance tail? No.

Actually, when the buffer is full, head and tail point to the same position, which is where the next read would happen, and also where the next write would go
But to overwrite, we want to replace the oldest element which is at head, and then make head point to the next oldest element
And tail should now point to the next write position, which is after the newly written data

So:
1. If not full, just write normally
2. If full, write to tail, which is the same as head, then advance both head and tail

Wait, but this means the new data is written where head is, and then head is advanced, making the next element the oldest
And tail is advanced to maintain the full state

Here's the fixed implementation:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Make space by moving head forward
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    }
    // Write the data
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    // Update full flag
    full = (tail == head);
}
=======
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Write the data to the current tail position, which will overwrite the oldest element
        buffer[tail] = data;
        // Advance both head and tail to maintain the full state
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        head = tail;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, this may not be exactly right. Let's test this approach:
When the buffer is full, head and tail are equal
We write data to tail, then advance tail
Then set head to tail, which makes them equal again, maintaining full=true
This seems to work

But according to the example in the instructions, when overwriting, the oldest data is replaced, and the new oldest becomes the next element
So after writing, head should point to the next element after the one that was just overwritten
So we need to advance head before or after writing

Wait, the correct approach is:
1. If the buffer is full, we need to move head forward first to make space for the new element
2. Then write the data to the current tail position
3. Then move tail forward
4. The buffer remains full because we're always writing when full

But this seems to match our initial approach, which had issues
Wait, the instructions say that when doing a forced write, the oldest data is overwritten
So the data at head should be replaced, and head should be advanced to point to the next oldest

So:
```cpp
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Replace the oldest element at head
        buffer[head] = data;
        // Move head to the next position
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        // Tail should also move to maintain consistency? No.
        // Since we're overwriting, the number of elements doesn't change, so tail should remain the same
        // But tail points to the next write position, which may need to be updated
        // This seems to conflict
        // Let's set tail to head to keep the buffer full
        tail = head;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
```

This seems to make sense. Let's use this implementation:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Write the data to the current tail position, which will overwrite the oldest element
        buffer[tail] = data;
        // Advance both head and tail to maintain the full state
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        head = tail;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
=======
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element at head
        buffer[head] = data;
        // Move head to the next position
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        // Update tail to maintain full state
        tail = head;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should now correctly handle overwriting by always replacing the oldest element when the buffer is full, and adjusting head and tail to maintain the buffer in a full state. When the buffer is not full, it simply uses the normal write operation.

I understand the issue. The tests are expecting a templated implementation, but our implementation is using `int` specifically. We need to make the implementation generic to handle any data type, including `std::string`. Let's fix that.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    size_t head;
    size_t tail;
    size_t capacity;
    bool full;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t size);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool is_full() const;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t head;
    size_t tail;
    size_t capacity;
    bool full;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t size);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool is_full() const;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    full = false;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (full) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    full = (tail == head);
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element at head
        buffer[head] = data;
        // Move head to the next position
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        // Update tail to maintain full state
        tail = head;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    full = false;
}

bool circular_buffer::empty() const {
    return (!full && (head == tail));
}

bool circular_buffer::is_full() const {
    return full;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    full = false;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    full = (tail == head);
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element at head
        buffer[head] = data;
        // Move head to the next position
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        // Update tail to maintain full state
        tail = head;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    full = false;
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::empty() const {
    return (!full && (head == tail));
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::is_full() const {
    return full;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for int and std::string to avoid linker errors
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<std::string>;

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

These changes will:
1. Make the implementation templated to handle any data type
2. Add explicit template instantiations for `int` and `std::string` to ensure the linker can find the implementations
3. Use `const T&` in write and overwrite to avoid unnecessary copies
4. Keep the core logic the same while making it generic

This should now work with the tests that use both integers and strings. The implementation follows the same approach as before, but now it's generic.

I understand. The issue is that the implementation needs to be in the header file because templates must be defined in the same file where they're declared. Let's move the implementation to the header file.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t head;
    size_t tail;
    size_t capacity;
    bool full;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t size);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool is_full() const;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t head;
    size_t tail;
    size_t capacity;
    bool full;

public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t size) 
        : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
    }

    T read() {
        if (empty()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer[head];
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        full = false;
        return value;
    }

    void write(const T& data) {
        if (full) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[tail] = data;
        tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
        full = (tail == head);
    }

    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full) {
            // Overwrite the oldest element at head
            buffer[head] = data;
            // Move head to the next position
            head = (head + 1) % capacity;
            // Update tail to maintain full state
            tail = head;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }

    void clear() {
        head = 0;
        tail = 0;
        full = false;
    }

    bool empty() const {
        return (!full && (head == tail));
    }

    bool is_full() const {
        return full;
    }
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
circular_buffer<T>::circular_buffer(size_t size) 
    : buffer(size), head(0), tail(0), capacity(size), full(false) {
}

template <typename T>
T circular_buffer<T>::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    T value = buffer[head];
    head = (head + 1) % capacity;
    full = false;
    return value;
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::write(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[tail] = data;
    tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
    full = (tail == head);
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::overwrite(const T& data) {
    if (full) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element at head
        buffer[head] = data;
        // Move head to the next position
        head = (head + 1) % capacity;
        // Update tail to maintain full state
        tail = head;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}

template <typename T>
void circular_buffer<T>::clear() {
    head = 0;
    tail = 0;
    full = false;
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::empty() const {
    return (!full && (head == tail));
}

template <typename T>
bool circular_buffer<T>::is_full() const {
    return full;
}

// Explicit template instantiation for int and std::string to avoid linker errors
template class circular_buffer<int>;
template class circular_buffer<std::string>;

}  // namespace circular_buffer

// This file can be empty or removed, but we'll keep it for now

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This change moves all the implementation into the header file, which is necessary for template classes. The .cpp file is now mostly empty, but we can keep it for consistency. The key points are:

1. Template implementations must be visible at the point of instantiation, so they need to be in the header
2. All member functions are now defined within the class definition in the header
3. This should resolve any linking issues with the template instantiations

This implementation should now work with the tests that use both integers and strings. Let me know if you encounter any further issues!

I understand. The implementation needs to be fixed to correctly handle the circular buffer operations, especially the `overwrite` function. The current implementation has an issue where when the buffer is full and we overwrite, it always sets `tail = head`, which may not be correct. Let's fix that.

Here's the correct approach for `overwrite`:
1. If the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element (at head)
2. Then advance head to make the next element the oldest
3. Write the new data at the current tail position
4. Advance tail
5. Since we're always writing when full, the buffer remains full

But actually, when overwriting, we're replacing the oldest element and making the next element the new oldest, then writing the new data where the next write would go
So we need to adjust head and tail correctly

Here are the necessary fixes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full) {
            // Overwrite the oldest element at head
            buffer[head] = data;
            // Move head to the next position
            head = (head + 1) % capacity;
            // Update tail to maintain full state
            tail = head;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
=======
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full) {
            // Overwrite the oldest element at head and advance head
            buffer[tail] = data;
            tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
            head = tail;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, this still may not be correct. Let's think through an example:
When the buffer is full, head and tail are at the same position
Overwriting should replace the element at head, then advance both head and tail
But this makes them equal again, which is correct for a full buffer

Wait, but the oldest element is at head, so to overwrite it, we should write at head and advance head
But then tail needs to be updated to head to maintain the full state

Actually, the correct implementation is:
1. If full, write at tail (which is the same as head when full)
2. Advance both head and tail to maintain full state
3. This effectively replaces the oldest element and makes the next element the new oldest

Wait, but when the buffer is full, head and tail are equal
So writing at tail is writing where head is
Then advancing both makes them equal again

This seems correct. Let's test this approach:

Wait, the implementation above writes at tail, advances tail, then sets head to tail
This is the same as:
buffer[tail] = data;
tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
head = tail;

Which when full, head and tail are equal, so:
1. Write at tail (head)
2. Advance tail
3. Set head to tail → they're equal again, maintaining full=true

But this seems to work. Let's proceed.

However, there's another issue: the `is_full()` function always returns the `full` flag, which may not be updated correctly in all cases
But in our implementation, we always update `full` when necessary

Wait, in the `overwrite` implementation above, we're not updating the `full` flag
But since the buffer remains full after overwriting, and `head == tail`, which is what `full` represents, we're good

Actually, the implementation is correct because:
1. When full, head == tail
2. We write to tail, advance tail, then set head to tail
3. So head == tail still, which means full remains true
4. The `full` member variable remains true, which matches `is_full()`

This should work. Let's make this change.

I understand. The issue is with the `overwrite` implementation. When the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element, which is at the `head` position, not at the `tail`. Let's fix that.

Here's the correct approach:
1. When the buffer is full, the oldest element is at `head`
2. We need to replace that element and advance `head` to make the next element the new oldest
3. Then write the new data at `tail` and advance `tail`
4. But since the buffer is full, `head` and `tail` are equal, so we need to be careful

Actually, a better approach is:
1. If the buffer is full, read and discard the oldest element to make space
2. Then write the new data normally
3. This way, we can reuse the existing `read()` and `write()` functions

Here's the fix:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full) {
            // Overwrite the oldest element at head and advance head
            buffer[tail] = data;
            tail = (tail + 1) % capacity;
            head = tail;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
=======
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full) {
            // Read and discard the oldest element to make space
            // This will advance head and set full to false
            read();
        }
        // Write the new data
        write(data);
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation is simpler and reuses existing functionality:
1. If the buffer is full, we remove the oldest element by calling `read()`
2. This advances `head` and sets `full` to false
3. Then we can write the new data normally using `write()`
4. The `write()` function will handle updating `tail` and setting `full` appropriately

This should now correctly handle overwriting by always removing the oldest element when the buffer is full before writing the new data. Let's see if this resolves the issues.
